26:881:63992:17:0:224:357:321:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:   
26:882:63998:0:32:477:495:329:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:    
26:883:64002:32:32:89:112:297:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(12) 
26:884:64007:32:21:89:486:265:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The observation in this regression is plant i in our firm data set. AGEi is the age of 
26:885:64094:21:21:89:504:244:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:plant i since its appearance in our firm data set. If it exits from our data set during our 
26:886:64186:21:21:89:511:223:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:study period, the dependent variable equals to 1, otherwise it equals to 0. There may be 
26:887:64275:21:20:89:482:202:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:several reasons for a plant’s exit: closure, relocation, or the size of its total output 
26:888:64364:20:21:89:510:182:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:shrinks to far below the threshold of the ASIFs survey (500 million RMB).15  Since we 
26:889:64450:21:21:89:499:161:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:do not know the reasons for why individual firms exit the sample, we assume that all 
26:890:64535:21:20:89:484:140:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sample exits represents a firm’s death.    Table A2 in the Appendix C  reports the 
26:891:64618:20:25:89:509:120:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:regression results of this probit model. Column (1) is for all plants. Older plants have a 
26:892:64709:25:7:89:235:95:11:g_d0_f1:11:g_d0_f1:F:                                                             
26:893:64769:7:14:89:495:88:6:g_d0_f3:9:g_d0_f3:F:15  Plants whose sales slip to a small extent below this threshold are not automatically removed from this sample 
26:894:64883:14:0:89:376:74:9:g_d0_f3:9:g_d0_f3:F:since the 5 million RMB is not a ‘hard’ rule (see details in Brandt et al. (2012)) 
27:895:64969:0:20:89:490:758:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:higher probability to be closed. We find that plants closer to industrial parks have a 
27:896:65056:20:21:89:504:738:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:lower probability to exit. This is another piece of evidence documenting the industrial 
27:897:65144:21:21:89:473:717:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:parks’ production spillovers. Interestingly, those plants closer to the city center, 
27:898:65229:21:20:89:504:696:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:universities and railway station have a higher probability to be closed. One possibility 
27:899:65318:20:21:89:495:676:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is that those places are undergoing urban redevelopment and industrial land uses are 
27:900:65403:21:21:89:493:655:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:replaced by commercial and residential land uses, so many manufacturing firms are 
27:901:65485:21:32:89:218:634:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:relocated to other places.   
27:902:65514:32:33:89:92:602:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B: 
27:903:65514:33:33:89:274:569:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:4.2  Heterogeneity in TFP spillovers 
27:904:65551:33:21:107:512:536:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f3:A: We now test for industrial park TFP spillover heterogeneity by allowing the TFP 
27:905:65631:21:20:89:512:515:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:spatial gradient to vary along four dimensions. The first dimension is based on the age 
27:906:65719:20:21:89:512:495:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of the park. We have two cohorts – old parks established before 1996 and new ones 
27:907:65801:21:21:89:513:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:established in or after 1996.    If the Chinese leaders built the best parks first and if 
27:908:65891:21:20:89:512:453:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:diminishing returns have taken place for subsequent parks then we will observe that the 
27:909:65979:20:21:89:512:433:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:new parks have weaker spillovers than the old ones.    We find evidence of diminishing 
27:910:66066:21:21:89:512:412:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:returns, the spatial gradient of the old parks’ TPF spillovers is 2.3 times that of the new 
27:911:66158:21:20:89:512:391:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:parks (-0.171 vs. -0.075).    Within each cohort, our panel data set of manufacturing 
27:912:66244:20:21:89:512:371:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:plants’ TFP allows us to examine as a park gets more mature, does its spillover effect 
27:913:66331:21:21:89:512:350:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:get larger. Panel B in Table 4 reports such heterogeneous spillovers. Within the old 
27:914:66416:21:21:89:512:329:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:park cohort, as a park matures over time, its TPF spillovers get stronger. For the new 
27:915:66503:21:20:89:512:308:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:parks, those with an age between 11-15 years also have much stronger spillovers than 
27:916:66588:20:21:89:512:288:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:younger ones.    The regression has the same specification as column (3) in Panel A 
27:917:66672:21:33:89:441:267:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(OLS regression with district-time trend and industry-year fixed effects). 
27:918:66747:33:20:107:513:234:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The  second  heterogeneity  depends  on  the  park’s  own  economic  power.  We 
27:919:66827:20:21:89:513:214:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:construct five “park power” indicators (powerpark,m, m=1,2,3,4,5): (1) park’s distance to 
27:920:66917:21:21:89:512:193:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the CBD. Closer distance means stronger linkage with the city’s mean economic center 
27:921:67002:21:20:89:512:172:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:so more powerful; (2) park’s size. Larger parks are more powerful; (3) the share of 
27:922:67086:20:21:89:512:152:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:SOE  employment  in  the  park.  SOEs  are  less  productive  so  smaller  share  of  SOEs 
27:923:67177:21:21:89:512:131:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:means more powerful parks; (4) the average human capital level (years to schooling) in 
27:924:67264:21:21:89:513:110:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the park. Higher human capital means more powerful; (5) the co-agglomeration index 
27:925:67347:21:0:89:512:89:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for the industries residing in the park, higher synergy between those industries will lead 
28:926:67441:0:20:89:513:758:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to a more powerful park.  Our hypothesis is that more powerful parks (measured by 
28:927:67523:20:33:89:312:738:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:these five indices) generate larger spillovers.   
28:928:67573:33:21:107:512:705:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The third heterogeneity dimension measures  the extent to which this park “fits” 
28:929:67654:21:20:89:512:684:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with the local incumbent industries. Following Glaeser and Kerr (2009), Ellison et al. 
28:930:67741:20:21:89:512:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(2010)  and  Jofre-Monseny  et  al.  (2011),  We  construct  four  park-vicinity  “synergy 
28:931:67832:21:21:89:512:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:indices” (synergypark-vicinity,n, n=1,2,3,4) to measure the input-output linkages, the size of 
28:932:67927:21:20:89:512:622:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:labor market pooling and the knowledge spillover possibility between within-park and 
28:933:68012:20:21:89:513:602:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:outside-park firms.  In Appendix B, we report the details of how we construct these 
28:934:68096:21:21:89:512:581:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:four indices. Our hypothesis here is that if an incumbent firm in a park’s vicinity has 
28:935:68184:21:21:89:512:560:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:higher synergy indices with the park, it will enjoy a larger spillover effect from the 
28:936:68271:21:32:89:122:539:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:park.   
28:937:68279:32:21:107:512:507:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The fourth heterogeneity depends on plant attributes. We construct two variables to 
28:938:68363:21:21:89:512:486:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:measure a plant’s size and age. Size is measured in a plant’s employment. We group all 
28:939:68450:21:20:89:512:465:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:plants into three age categories based on their establishment year: before 1978 (before 
28:940:68538:20:21:89:513:445:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the economic reform), between 1979 and 1998 (earlier stage of the economic reform) 
28:941:68621:21:21:89:297:424:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f4:B:and after 1998 (later stage of the reform).  
28:942:68665:21:20:110:509:403:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We estimate Equation (13) to    (15) to explore the heterogeneity in the spatial decay 
28:943:68752:20:21:89:489:383:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rate of TFP spillovers with respect to the second to the fourth sets of heterogeneity 
28:944:68838:21:25:89:140:362:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:measures.

29:1019:69573:0:20:89:512:758:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Table 5 reports the heterogeneity TFP spillovers results. In the first three columns we 
29:1020:69661:20:21:89:513:738:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:interact the four park-vicinity synergy indices with log(DISTANCE_PARK). In column 
29:1021:69744:21:21:89:512:717:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(1) with all plants, higher input linkage and output linkage, as well as stronger skill 
29:1022:69832:21:20:89:512:696:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:spillover  between  within-park  and  outside-park  plants  will  lead  to  larger  park  TFP 
29:1023:69926:20:21:89:512:676:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:spillovers. We only keep those plants with small zone identifier in column (2) and then 
29:1024:70014:21:21:89:512:655:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:further  include  plant  fixed  effects  in  column  (3),  and  the  output  linkage  index  is 
29:1025:70110:21:20:89:512:634:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:statistically significant. All the four synergy indices are jointly significant in the three 
29:1026:70203:20:21:89:512:614:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:columns, indicating that those parks that are better “fit” into their vicinity in terms of 
29:1027:70294:21:21:89:512:593:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:industry synergies can generate higher TFP spillovers.    In columns (4)-(6) we interact 
29:1028:70383:21:21:89:512:572:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the five park power indices with log(DISTANCE_PARK). Distance to CBD does not 
29:1029:70461:21:20:89:512:551:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:influence  this  gradient  significantly,  while  the  other  four  power  indices  have  some 
29:1030:70556:20:21:89:512:531:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:impacts  and  have  the  right  signs.  These  five  interaction  terms  are  also  jointly 
29:1031:70648:21:21:89:512:510:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:significant,  showing  that  more  powerful  parks  lead  to  higher  spillover  effects.  In 
29:1032:70742:21:20:89:512:489:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:columns  (7)-(9)  we  interact  plant  size  (employment)  and  age  group  dummies  with 
29:1033:70832:20:21:89:512:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:log(DISTANCE_PARK). Smaller and younger plants enjoy higher TFP spillovers from 
29:1034:70912:21:33:89:157:448:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:nearby parks.

29:1037:70960:35:35:89:331:348:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:5. Estimating Consumption Spillovers   
29:1038:70998:35:32:89:413:313:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:5.1  The Increase in Consumer Market Potential in Edge Cities 
29:1039:71060:32:21:110:498:281:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The productivity increase both inside the park and in its vicinity will attract new 
29:1040:71144:21:20:89:489:260:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:entrants, and the incumbent firms will also expand their employment.    A growing 
29:1041:71226:20:21:89:467:240:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:workforce that seeks a short commute to work will seek out housing and retail 
29:1042:71304:21:21:89:476:219:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:opportunities near the new industrial park. All together the market potential will 
29:1043:71387:21:21:89:496:198:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:increase and thus trigger new housing construction and retail activities in those edge 
29:1044:71474:21:32:89:120:177:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cities. 
29:1045:71482:32:21:110:511:145:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:To measure these effects, we estimate equations (16) and (17) where the dependent 
29:1046:71564:21:21:89:497:124:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:variable is the manufacturing employment density EMP. The unit of analysis here is 
29:1047:71646:21:20:89:494:103:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:zone k.    In estimating these regressions, in one specification we use the data for all 
29:1048:71735:20:0:89:506:83:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:zones and in a second we focus on the subset of zones outside parks. For the latter, we 
30:1049:71826:0:20:89:500:758:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:control for the global impact of other parks in the city, and focus on the impact of the 
30:1050:71915:20:36:89:288:738:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:closest park. See Equation (16)  and (17).

30:1089:73515:33:32:89:235:229:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:5.2  Home Sales and Pricing 
30:1090:73543:32:21:110:472:197:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In many major Chinese cities, the center city is the most vibrant part of the 
30:1091:73621:21:21:89:509:176:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:metropolitan area.    Similar to major European cities, jobs, government, and amenities 
30:1092:73709:21:21:89:508:155:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are clustered downtown (Brueckner, Thisse and Zenou 1999).    Given the attraction of 
30:1093:73795:21:20:89:508:134:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the city center, real estate prices are quite high close to the downtown and decline with 
30:1094:73885:20:0:89:350:114:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:distance from the downtown (Zheng and Kahn 2008). 
31:1095:73938:0:20:110:462:758:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Chinese mayors seek to encourage economic growth in other parts of the 
31:1096:74009:20:21:89:504:738:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:metropolitan area. As we documented in Table 2, a typical industrial park is located at 
31:1097:74097:21:21:89:506:717:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the edge of the urban area whose previous use as agriculture land.    The emergence of 
31:1098:74184:21:20:89:481:696:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:this new edge city and the rising purchase power of consumers will generate new 
31:1099:74264:20:21:89:454:676:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:demand for housing and local consumption goods, and thus trigger housing 
31:1100:74337:21:21:89:493:655:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:development and the opening of new retail stores nearby, as shown in Figure 3. The 
31:1101:74420:21:20:89:504:634:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:main land use type within industrial parks is industrial land, so managers and workers 
31:1102:74507:20:21:89:502:614:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in those plants will buy or rent residential units outside but near the park. That is why 
31:1103:74597:21:21:89:485:593:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in Figure 3 we see the closest zones to parks have the highest densities of housing 
31:1104:74681:21:33:89:421:572:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:transactions in the surrounding area, even higher than that in parks.   
31:1105:74753:33:20:110:512:539:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:To empirically test whether there is a booming housing market around the park, we 
31:1106:74835:20:21:89:502:519:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:construct two dependent variables – the number of new home sales in the 2 km*2 km 
31:1107:74917:21:21:89:486:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:grid cell g by quarter (HOUSE_SALESgt), and the transaction price in a residential 
31:1108:75000:21:20:89:501:477:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:complex l by quarter (HOUSE_PRICElt). We use each complex’s exact street address 
31:1109:75081:20:21:89:497:457:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to calculate its shortest real travel distance to the closest park’s boundary. We expect 
31:1110:75170:21:21:89:501:436:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that, controlling for the real travel distance to the main center (CBD), those grid cells 
31:1111:75260:21:20:89:505:415:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:closer to a park will see more new home sales, and we should also observe that homes 
31:1112:75345:20:21:89:496:395:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:closer to the park sell for a price premium. We control for the global impact of other 
31:1113:75432:21:37:89:308:374:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:parks in the city. See Equation (18) and (19).

32:1147:76242:0:20:89:506:758:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for distance to the CBD, we observe a negative gradient with respect to the distance to 
32:1148:76330:20:21:89:508:738:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the closest park (as a subcenter). The size of this spatial decay rate is quite large, about 
32:1149:76423:21:21:89:509:717:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:-0.221 (log-log). Note that the price gradient with respect to the distance to the CBD is 
32:1150:76513:21:20:89:483:696:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:insignificant here. In the ZIP-IV regression (column (2)), this decay rate becomes 
32:1151:76596:20:21:89:508:676:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:smaller (-0.199)  , and it is statistically significant at 1% level, indicating there may be 
32:1152:76689:21:21:89:480:655:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:some unobserved location attributes that are positively related to both residential 
32:1153:76773:21:20:89:507:634:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:development activities and the location choice of an industrial park. The global impact 
32:1154:76861:20:21:89:498:614:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of other parks on local housing sales is also statistically significant but the economic 
32:1155:76950:21:33:89:160:593:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:size is small.   
32:1156:76967:33:21:110:503:560:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Column (3) tells us that residential units close to the parks further from the CBD,

32:1160:77232:33:20:110:497:465:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Columns (4) – (6) report hedonic housing price regressions (Equation (18)). We 
32:1161:77311:20:21:89:499:445:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:control for a residential complex’s physical attributes such as its construction density

32:1163:77487:21:20:89:483:403:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:significantly negative gradient of housing price with respect to the distance to the 
32:1164:77572:20:21:89:485:383:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:nearby park. This housing price decay rate is about -0.101 (log-log) in column (4) 
32:1165:77655:21:21:89:504:362:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(OLS), and its absolute value also shrinks in the IV regression in column (5) (-0.095). 
32:1166:77743:21:21:89:507:341:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The magnitude of this local gradient is about 55% of the global price gradient (-0.170) 
32:1167:77831:21:20:89:484:320:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with respect to the distance to the CBD. The global impact of other parks on local 
32:1168:77914:20:21:89:502:300:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:housing prices is also statistically significant and has a big economic size– a standard 
32:1169:78003:21:21:89:500:279:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:deviation increase in GLOBAL_PARK_IMPACT can induce a 0.55 standard deviation 
32:1170:78081:21:20:89:491:258:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:increase in local housing sales.    Larger parks, parks with higher co-agglomeration 
32:1171:78166:20:21:89:511:238:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:index, higher human capital, less SOE employment are more attractive to home buyers. 
32:1172:78251:21:33:89:472:217:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The five heterogeneity measures of a park’s power are also jointly significant.

33:1200:79465:21:20:89:512:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:these  three  consumption  amenities  shrink  in  IV  regressions.  The  local  gradient 
33:1201:79554:20:21:89:512:485:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:generated by the closest park is about a quarter of the global gradient generated by the 
33:1202:79643:21:21:89:512:464:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:main center for all the three amenity types. The global impact of other parks on the 
33:1203:79728:21:21:89:512:443:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:quantity of consumption amenities is statistically significant but the economic sizes are 
33:1204:79818:21:20:89:512:422:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:small. We again find that parks further away from the CBD and parks with larger size 
33:1205:79903:20:21:89:512:402:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:have  larger  gentrification  effects.  The  five  heterogeneity  measures  of  a  park’s 
33:1206:79993:21:33:89:469:381:12:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f2:B:economic power are also jointly significant for these three local private goods. 
33:1207:80073:33:32:219:383:348:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:*** Insert Table 8 about here *** 
33:1208:80107:32:21:89:513:316:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:    Recall that the coefficients of DISTANCE_PARK in TFP equations become larger 
33:1209:80188:21:21:89:512:295:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in IV regressions compared to those in OLS regressions. Here for housing and retail 
33:1210:80272:21:20:89:512:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equations,  we  find  such  coefficients  all  shrink  from  OLS  to  IV  regressions  in  TFP 
33:1211:80367:20:21:89:512:254:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equations.  This  indicates  that,  city  mayors  locate  parks  in  those  places  with  larger 
33:1212:80464:21:21:89:512:233:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:consumption potential, but smaller production potential. One possible explanation for 
33:1213:80550:21:21:89:512:212:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:city  mayors’  intension  behind  this  park  location  decision  is  that,  city  mayors  can 
33:1214:80645:21:20:89:512:191:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:receive higher land sale revenue by selling the residential and commercial land parcels 
33:1215:80733:20:21:89:512:171:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:near industrial parks if the parks’ consumption spillovers are large. Housing and retail 
33:1216:80822:21:21:89:512:150:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are non-tradable goods. Instead, city mayors have to set very low price for industrial 
33:1217:80909:21:20:89:512:129:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:land parcels in parks and also provide tax break in the initial years to attract mobile 
33:1218:80997:20:21:89:512:109:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:firms. Chinese city mayors have a term constraint (four years for one term. A mayor 
33:1219:81081:21:0:89:512:88:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:always  stay  in  position  for  one  to  two  terms).  From  the  mayor’s  perspective,  the 
34:1220:81178:0:20:89:512:758:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:revenue  from  residential  and  commercial  land  sales  can  be  realized  in  a  lump-sum 
34:1221:81271:20:21:89:512:738:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:form  in  the  short-run,  while  tax  revenue  from  productive  firms  can  only  come  in 
34:1222:81364:21:21:89:512:717:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:annually in the long-term, so they have the incentive to place parks in those places with 
34:1223:81454:21:34:89:236:696:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:higher consumption potential. 
34:1224:81484:34:34:89:177:662:14:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:B:6. Conclusion 
34:1225:81496:34:21:107:509:628:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:At the broadest level, our paper provides strong support for Marshallian theories of 
34:1226:81581:21:21:89:479:607:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:localized production and consumption co-agglomeration in a leading developing 
34:1227:81659:21:21:89:490:586:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:country. Using the opening of over 120 industrial parks across eight major Chinese 
34:1228:81742:21:20:89:495:565:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cities as a natural experiment, we quantify the spatial decay patterns in productivity, 
34:1229:81830:20:21:89:503:545:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:firm survival, real estate construction, real estate pricing, and retail store openings for 
34:1230:81922:21:21:89:508:524:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:economic activity close to these new suburban centers of productivity. Consistent with 
34:1231:82009:21:20:89:488:503:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Marshall’s core hypotheses, we find that proximity to the parks reduce the costs of 
34:1232:82093:20:33:89:265:483:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:moving goods, people, and ideas.   
34:1233:82127:33:21:107:498:450:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Unlike other agglomeration studies, we have explicitly integrated our analysis of 
34:1234:82209:21:20:89:478:429:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the production and consumption side of the economy.   The new park creates a 
34:1235:82286:20:21:89:485:409:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:spatially concentrated increase in local market potential as well paid workers seek 
34:1236:82370:21:21:89:503:388:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:nearby housing and retail opportunities. We have provided new evidence on this local 
34:1237:82455:21:21:89:508:367:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:multiplier effect in a developing nation (Moretti 2010).  This local multiplier effect is 
34:1238:82545:21:32:89:516:346:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:larger for those industrial parks that attract more human capital and more private firms.   
34:1239:82637:32:21:107:504:314:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We have explicitly modeled the tradeoffs that the mayor faces in siting a new park 
34:1240:82720:21:21:89:465:293:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in a specific area within a city.    A forward looking mayor has an incentive to 
34:1241:82801:21:20:89:486:272:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:recognize that each area in a city may offer different benefits and impose different 
34:1242:82886:20:21:89:472:252:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:costs if a park is built there.    When we use cost shifter proxies as instrumental 
34:1243:82970:21:21:89:484:231:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:variables, we estimate a larger TFP treatment effect from building a park. But, we 
34:1244:83053:21:21:89:497:210:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:estimate smaller IV estimates in our housing and retail regressions.    This collective 
34:1245:83141:21:20:89:464:189:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:set of facts suggests that mayors locate parks in those places featuring greater 
34:1246:83222:20:33:89:404:169:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:consumption potential but lower producer efficiency potential.     
34:1247:83289:33:21:107:494:136:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:One explanation for these facts is due to the Chinese political system.    Chinese 
34:1248:83372:21:20:89:495:115:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mayors face term limits so that they serve for at most eight years. From the mayor’s 
34:1249:83457:20:0:89:505:95:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:perspective, the revenue from residential and commercial land sales can be realized in 
35:1250:83547:0:20:89:497:758:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a lump   -sum form in the short-run, while tax revenue from productive firms can only 
35:1251:83633:20:21:89:496:738:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:come in annually in the long-term, so they have the incentive to place parks in those 
35:1252:83719:21:33:89:293:717:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:places with higher consumption potential. 
35:1253:83760:33:32:107:110:684:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A: 
35:1254:83760:32:21:107:110:652:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A: 
35:1255:83760:21:21:89:92:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B: 
35:1256:83760:21:20:89:113:610:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:     
35:1257:83765:20:21:89:92:590:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B: 
35:1258:83765:21:0:89:236:569:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:

57:2070:117935:0:15:89:158:757:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:Appendix A   
57:2071:117948:15:15:89:500:742:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:Constructing Plant-level TFP and Park-level Co-   agglomeration Index Measures 
57:2072:118027:15:17:89:92:727:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:F: 
57:2073:118027:17:31:89:282:710:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:Constructing plant-level TFP measure 
57:2074:118064:31:15:89:512:679:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:To  estimate  the  plant-level  TFP,  we  first  consider  a  firm  with  a  Cobb-Douglas 
57:2075:118154:15:35:89:190:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:production function, 
57:2076:118175:35:7:136:171:629:4:g_d0_f5:4:g_d0_f5:F:lk
57:2077:118177:7:0:96:147:622:6:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:F:itit  it   itY   A L K
57:2078:118199:0:45:131:221:631:6:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f3:A:      (A1) 
57:2079:118213:45:16:89:513:586:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Where Yit is output for plant i at time t, which is the function of labor, L, and capital, K. 
57:2080:118306:16:15:89:512:570:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:A(τ)  measures  the  extent  to  which  local  public  infrastructure, τ,  enhances  a  plant’s 
57:2081:118402:15:32:89:153:555:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:productivity. 
57:2082:118416:32:41:89:383:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Then we take the natural logs of equation (A1) and estimate: 
57:2083:118477:41:37:132:307:482:6:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:0lnlnlnitlitkititYLK                (A2) 
57:2084:118528:37:15:89:512:445:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The dependent variable is real value added at the plant level, which is constructed by 
57:2085:118615:15:16:89:512:430:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:separately deflating output, net of goods purchased for resale and indirect taxes, and 
57:2086:118702:16:15:89:512:414:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:material inputs. Labor input, L, is measured by the number of employees each year. 
57:2087:118785:15:16:89:512:399:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Capital  stock  is  measured  by  plant-level  real  book  value  of  fixed  assets.  The 
57:2088:118875:16:16:89:513:383:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:information on plants’ fixed investment is not available in the ASIFs dataset, which 
57:2089:118960:16:15:89:513:367:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reports the value of plants’ fixed capital stocks at original purchase price, and their 
57:2090:119048:15:16:89:512:352:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:capital  stock  at  original  purchase  prices  less  accumulated  depreciation.  These  book 
57:2091:119142:16:15:89:512:336:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:values are the sum of nominal values and are not comparable across time and firms. 
57:2092:119225:15:16:89:513:321:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We follow the procedure developed by Brandt et al (2012) and estimate plants’ real 
57:2093:119308:16:16:89:513:305:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:value of the capital stock in each year. εit is the error term, which has two components, 
57:2094:119398:16:31:89:440:289:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a white noise component, ηit, and a time-varying productivity shock, ωit. 
57:2095:119471:31:15:89:512:258:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:A  major  concern  in  estimating  equation  (A2)  is  that  the  correlation  between 
57:2096:119558:15:16:89:513:243:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:unobservable productivity shocks, ωit, and the input factors chosen by the plant. This 
57:2097:119645:16:16:89:512:227:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:may produce inconsistent estimates under OLS. A second problem is the endogeneity 
57:2098:119727:16:15:89:512:211:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:arising  from  sample  selection.  Plants  exit  when  productivity  falls  below  a  certain 
57:2099:119821:15:16:89:513:196:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:threshold, and thus the surviving firms will have ωit from the selected sample, which 
57:2100:119907:16:15:89:512:180:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:has an effect on the inputs employed. To address both of these two problems, we rely 
57:2101:119992:15:16:89:512:165:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on Olley-Pakes (OP) estimator (Olley and Pakes 1996). We estimate the production 
57:2102:120073:16:16:89:512:149:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:function for  plants  in  each two-digit sectors separately  with  Olley-Pakes.  Thus, the 
57:2103:120164:16:37:89:342:133:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:measured TFP of plant i i n year t, tfpit, is defined as: 
57:2104:120222:37:0:185:315:96:11:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:ˆˆlog()  lnlnlnititlitkitTFPYLK          (A3) 
58:2105:120278:0:15:89:512:757:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The  estimated  inputs  coefficients  obtained  from  estimating  equation  (A2)  with 
58:2106:120365:15:16:89:512:742:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Olley-Pakes are presented in Table A1. For comparison we also report OLS estimates 
58:2107:120448:16:15:89:512:726:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with  different  production  coefficients.  The  correlation  between  the  OP  and  OLS  is 
58:2108:120541:15:16:89:512:711:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:quite high: 0.976 in value. Both of the labor and capital estimates are underestimated 
58:2109:120628:16:16:89:512:695:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with OLS, as expected when unobserved productivity is also possibly correlated with 
58:2110:120712:16:20:89:257:679:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:labor inputs and real capital stock. 
58:2111:120749:20:21:89:92:659:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:F: 
58:2112:120749:21:20:89:330:638:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:F:Table A1 Firm-level production estimation results

60:2165:122024:0:15:89:381:757:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:Appendix B Constructing Park-Vicinity Synergy Indices 
60:2166:122078:15:31:89:92:742:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:F: 
60:2167:122078:31:16:89:513:711:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We aim to identify the sources of an industrial park’s spillover effect on the nearby 
60:2168:122164:16:16:89:512:695:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:incumbent  firms.  Following  Glaeser  and  Kerr  (2009),  Ellison  et  al.  (2010),  and 
60:2169:122254:16:15:89:512:679:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Jofre-Monseny  et  al.(2011),  our  first  step  is  to  construct  measures  of  the  extent  to 
60:2170:122352:15:16:89:512:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:which two industries (1) have a strong input-and-output linkage; (2) share the same 
60:2171:122436:16:15:89:512:648:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:type of workers ; or (3) have a higher probability of knowledge spillovers. The second 
60:2172:122523:15:16:89:512:633:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:step is, for a specific industry an outside-park firm belongs to, we construct industry 
60:2173:122611:16:16:89:512:617:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:pairs  by  matching  this  industry  with  all  the  industries  within  the  park,  and  then 
60:2174:122706:16:15:89:512:601:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:computing the weighted sum of the above industry-pair measures (the weight is set to 
60:2175:122791:15:31:89:518:586:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:be the employment share of that within-park industry in the whole park’s employment).   
60:2176:122879:31:16:89:513:555:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We first measure the advantage that a firm exploits from locating close to a park rife 
60:2177:122966:16:16:89:513:539:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with potential input suppliers and output demanders. The variables Inputr←q is defined 
60:2178:123053:16:15:89:513:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as the share of industry r’s inputs come from industry q, and Onputr→q as the share of 
60:2179:123140:15:16:89:513:508:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:industry r’s goes to industry q. These two measures range from zero to one since they 
60:2180:123226:16:15:89:512:492:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are calculated relative to all input suppliers and output demanders. We calculate these 
60:2181:123314:15:16:89:512:477:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:two variables for two-digit-level manufacturing sectors using the input-output flows 
60:2182:123399:16:16:89:512:461:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:information  according  to  the  2002  China  Input-Output  Tables  published  by  China 
60:2183:123488:16:31:89:195:445:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Bureau of Statistics.   
60:2184:123512:31:15:89:512:414:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Based on these two variables, the first synergy index measures the impact of a park j in
